# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# HTTP Health Check Endpoint Conventions Across Go Projects

## Your Task

Find and compare how /healthz and /readyz endpoints are implemented across kubernetes/kubernetes, grafana/grafana, and prometheus/prometheus. Identify the Go source files in each repo that register these endpoints and what checks each performs (DB, cache, dependencies).

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

65-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the `/healthz` and `/readyz` endpoint implementations across all three repositories. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Discoveries

**Kubernetes (kubernetes/kubernetes):**
- Uses 3 endpoints: `/healthz`, `/livez`, `/readyz`
- Sophisticated pluggable health check system via `HealthChecker` interface
- Performs checks on: etcd connectivity, informer cache sync, logging, and shutdown signals
- Located in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/healthz/`

**Grafana (grafana/grafana):**
- Uses 2 endpoints: `/livez`, `/readyz`
- Simple binary readiness state using `HealthNotifier` with `atomic.Bool`
- Operators explicitly signal readiness via `SetReady()`
- Located in `pkg/server/health.go`

**Prometheus (prometheus/prometheus):**
- Uses different naming: `/-/healthy`, `/-/ready` (with `/-/` prefix)
- State machine with 3 states: `NotReady`, `Ready`, `Stopping`
- Checks TSDB (Time Series Database) readiness
- Returns HTTP header `X-Prometheus-Stopping` for graceful shutdown signaling
- Located in `web/web.go`

The answer file at `/workspace/answer.json` contains all relevant files, symbols, call chains, and detailed comparison documentation of these implementations.

readiness via `NamedGroupedCheck(\\\"etcd-readiness\\\", \\\"etcd-readiness\\\", ...)`\\n- **Informers:** Verify all informers have synced caches\\n- **Shutdown Signal:** Track graceful shutdown state\\n\\n**Architecture:**\\nKubernetes uses a health check registry pattern where multiple checks are collected and installed via `InstallPathHandler()`. The system supports excluding checks via query parameters (`?exclude=check-name`) and verbose output (`?verbose=1`). Each registry (healthz, livez, readyz) maintains independent check lists with optional grace periods for livez during boot sequences.\\n\\n### Grafana (grafana/grafana)\\n\\nGrafana implements a minimal health endpoint system focused on operator readiness signaling.\\n\\n**Endpoints:** `/livez`, `/readyz`\\n\\n**Key Files:**\\n- `pkg/server/health.go` - Health endpoint handlers and HealthNotifier state management\\n- `pkg/services/apiserver/service.go` - Endpoint registration via gorilla/mux\\n\\n**Key Symbols:**\\n- `HealthNotifier` struct - Thread-safe state holder using `atomic.Bool`\\n- `LivezHandler()` - Always returns 200 OK (process is alive)\\n- `ReadyzHandler(h *HealthNotifier)` - Returns 200 OK if ready, 503 if not ready\\n- `RegisterHealthEndpoints()` - Registers both endpoints on provided router\\n- `SetReady()`, `SetNotReady()`, `IsReady()` - State management methods\\n\\n**Dependency Checks:**\\nGrafana uses a simple binary readiness state managed by operators. No automatic dependency checks for databases or caches. Instead, operators explicitly signal readiness via `SetReady()` after completing initialization.\\n\\n**Architecture:**\\nGrafana's approach is intentionally simple: livez always succeeds (indicating the HTTP server is running), while readyz returns success only when the operator has explicitly called `SetReady()`. This allows operators to perform their own initialization checks and signal completion. The health state is shared across the InstrumentationServer and OperatorServer via a single shared `HealthNotifier` instance.\\n\\n### Prometheus (prometheus/prometheus)\\n\\nPrometheus implements health endpoints with TSDB readiness gating and graceful shutdown support.\\n\\n**Endpoints:** `/-/healthy`, `/-/ready` (note: different path prefix convention)\\n\\n**Key Files:**\\n- `web/web.go` - Handler definition, ReadyStatus state machine, and endpoint registration\\n\\n**Key Symbols:**\\n- `ReadyStatus` enum with three states: `NotReady` (iota = 0), `Ready` (= 1), `Stopping` (= 2)\\n- `testReady()` method - Wraps handlers with readiness checks\\n- `isReady()` - Returns true if ReadyStatus == Ready\\n- `setReady()`, `setNotReady()`, `setStopping()` - State transition methods\\n- Metrics: `prometheus_ready` gauge tracks readiness state\\n\\n**Dependency Checks:**\\n- **TSDB Readiness:** The ready endpoint checks if TSDB (Time Series Database) has completed initialization\\n- **Graceful Shutdown:** Returns 503 when in Stopping state (signaling removal from load balancers while keeping liveness checks passing)\\n\\n**Architecture:**\\nPrometheus uses a state machine approach with three states. The `/-/healthy` endpoint (HEAD and GET support) always succeeds, while `/-/ready` (also HEAD and GET) wraps handlers with `testReady()` middleware that:\\n- Returns 200 OK if Ready\\n- Returns 503 Service Unavailable with `X-Prometheus-Stopping: false` if NotReady\\n- Returns 503 Service Unavailable with `X-Prometheus-Stopping: true` if Stopping\\n\\nThis allows clients to distinguish between \\\"not yet ready\\\" and \\\"actively shutting down\\\" scenarios. The ready endpoint also guards API endpoints like `/federate` and `/consoles` to prevent serving traffic during startup or shutdown.\\n\\n### Comparison Summary\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | Grafana | Prometheus |\\n|--------|-----------|---------|------------|\\n| **Endpoints** | /healthz, /livez, /readyz | /livez, /readyz | /-/healthy, /-/ready |\\n| **DB Checks** | Yes (etcd via NamedGroupedCheck) | No (manual) | Implicit (TSDB readiness) |\\n| **Cache/Informer Checks** | Yes (NewInformerSyncHealthz) | No | No |\\n| **Pluggable Checks** | Yes (HealthChecker interface) | No (binary state only) | No |\\n| **Shutdown Handling** | Explicit NewShutdownHealthz | No | Stopping state with header |\\n| **Grace Periods** | Yes (livez grace period) | No | No |\\n| **Query Parameters** | Yes (?exclude, ?verbose) | No | No |\\n\\n**Common Patterns:**\\n- All three separate liveness (/livez or /-/healthy) from readiness (/readyz or /-/ready)\\n- Readiness checks block traffic during startup\\n- Support for HTTP HEAD requests in addition to GET\\n- Graceful shutdown integration (explicit in Kubernetes/Prometheus, implicit in Grafana via SetNotReady)\"\n}\n",

state\\n\\n**Architecture:**\\nKubernetes uses a health check registry pattern where multiple checks are collected and installed via `InstallPathHandler()`. The system supports excluding checks via query parameters (`?exclude=check-name`) and verbose output (`?verbose=1`). Each registry (healthz, livez, readyz) maintains independent check lists with optional grace periods for livez during boot sequences.\\n\\n### Grafana (grafana/grafana)\\n\\nGrafana implements a minimal health endpoint system focused on operator readiness signaling.\\n\\n**Endpoints:** `/livez`, `/readyz`\\n\\n**Key Files:**\\n- `pkg/server/health.go` - Health endpoint handlers and HealthNotifier state management\\n- `pkg/services/apiserver/service.go` - Endpoint registration via gorilla/mux\\n\\n**Key Symbols:**\\n- `HealthNotifier` struct - Thread-safe state holder using `atomic.Bool`\\n- `LivezHandler()` - Always returns 200 OK (process is alive)\\n- `ReadyzHandler(h *HealthNotifier)` - Returns 200 OK if ready, 503 if not ready\\n- `RegisterHealthEndpoints()` - Registers both endpoints on provided router\\n- `SetReady()`, `SetNotReady()`, `IsReady()` - State management methods\\n\\n**Dependency Checks:**\\nGrafana uses a simple binary readiness state managed by operators. No automatic dependency checks for databases or caches. Instead, operators explicitly signal readiness via `SetReady()` after completing initialization.\\n\\n**Architecture:**\\nGrafana's approach is intentionally simple: livez always succeeds (indicating the HTTP server is running), while readyz returns success only when the operator has explicitly called `SetReady()`. This allows operators to perform their own initialization checks and signal completion. The health state is shared across the InstrumentationServer and OperatorServer via a single shared `HealthNotifier` instance.\\n\\n### Prometheus (prometheus/prometheus)\\n\\nPrometheus implements health endpoints with TSDB readiness gating and graceful shutdown support.\\n\\n**Endpoints:** `/-/healthy`, `/-/ready` (note: different path prefix convention)\\n\\n**Key Files:**\\n- `web/web.go` - Handler definition, ReadyStatus state machine, and endpoint registration\\n\\n**Key Symbols:**\\n- `ReadyStatus` enum with three states: `NotReady` (iota = 0), `Ready` (= 1), `Stopping` (= 2)\\n- `testReady()` method - Wraps handlers with readiness checks\\n- `isReady()` - Returns true if ReadyStatus == Ready\\n- `setReady()`, `setNotReady()`, `setStopping()` - State transition methods\\n- Metrics: `prometheus_ready` gauge tracks readiness state\\n\\n**Dependency Checks:**\\n- **TSDB Readiness:** The ready endpoint checks if TSDB (Time Series Database) has completed initialization\\n- **Graceful Shutdown:** Returns 503 when in Stopping state (signaling removal from load balancers while keeping liveness checks passing)\\n\\n**Architecture:**\\nPrometheus uses a state machine approach with three states. The `/-/healthy` endpoint (HEAD and GET support) always succeeds, while `/-/ready` (also HEAD and GET) wraps handlers with `testReady()` middleware that:\\n- Returns 200 OK if Ready\\n- Returns 503 Service Unavailable with `X-Prometheus-Stopping: false` if NotReady\\n- Returns 503 Service Unavailable with `X-Prometheus-Stopping: true` if Stopping\\n\\nThis allows clients to distinguish between \\\"not yet ready\\\" and \\\"actively shutting down\\\" scenarios. The ready endpoint also guards API endpoints like `/federate` and `/consoles` to prevent serving traffic during startup or shutdown.\\n\\n### Comparison Summary\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | Grafana | Prometheus |\\n|--------|-----------|---------|------------|\\n| **Endpoints** | /healthz, /livez, /readyz | /livez, /readyz | /-/healthy, /-/ready |\\n| **DB Checks** | Yes (etcd via NamedGroupedCheck) | No (manual) | Implicit (TSDB readiness) |\\n| **Cache/Informer Checks** | Yes (NewInformerSyncHealthz) | No | No |\\n| **Pluggable Checks** | Yes (HealthChecker interface) | No (binary state only) | No |\\n| **Shutdown Handling** | Explicit NewShutdownHealthz | No | Stopping state with header |\\n| **Grace Periods** | Yes (livez grace period) | No | No |\\n| **Query Parameters** | Yes (?exclude, ?verbose) | No | No |\\n\\n**Common Patterns:**\\n- All three separate liveness (/livez or /-/healthy) from readiness (/readyz or /-/ready)\\n- Readiness checks block traffic during startup\\n- Support for HTTP HEAD requests in addition to GET\\n- Graceful shutdown integration (explicit in Kubernetes/Prometheus, implicit in Grafana via SetNotReady)\"\n}\n",
